</tr>

<p><i><b>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</b></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[b]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Open_world" title="Open world">open world</a> <a href="/wiki/Action-adventure_game" title="Action-adventure game">action-adventure</a> <a href="/wiki/Stealth_game" title="Stealth game">stealth</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Kojima_Productions" title="Kojima Productions">Kojima Productions</a> and published by <a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a> for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>. It was released worldwide on September 1, 2015. It is the ninth and final installment in the series directed, written and designed by <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a> following <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_Ground_Zeroes" title="Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes">Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes</a></i>, a stand-alone prologue released the previous year, as well as his final work prior to his departure from Konami.</p>
<p>Set in 1984, nine years after the events of <i>Ground Zeroes</i> and a decade before the events of the original <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(video_game)" title="Metal Gear (video game)">Metal Gear</a></i>, the story follows mercenary leader <a href="/wiki/Venom_Snake" title="Venom Snake">Venom Snake</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a>) as he ventures into <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a>-occupied <a href="/wiki/Kabul_Province" title="Kabul Province">Kabul Province</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>–<a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> border region to exact revenge on the people who destroyed his forces and came close to killing him during the climax of <i>Ground Zeroes</i>. It carries over the tagline of <i>Tactical Espionage Operations</i> first used in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Peace_Walker" title="Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker">Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker</a></i>.</p>
<p><i>The Phantom Pain</i> was critically acclaimed upon release, with its gameplay drawing praise for featuring a variety of <a href="/wiki/Game_mechanics" title="Game mechanics">mechanics</a> and interconnected systems which allow a high degree of player freedom in approaching objectives. While the story drew criticism from a few reviewers for its lack of focus, others acknowledged its emotional power and exploration of mature <a href="/wiki/Theme_(narrative)" title="Theme (narrative)">themes</a>. The game received perfect review scores from several publications, including <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> and <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>, and was described by some critics as the best stealth game ever made. A complete edition, titled <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Definitive Experience</i>, which bundles both <i>The Phantom Pain</i> and <i>Ground Zeroes</i> together, was released in October 2016.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In <i>The Phantom Pain</i>, players take the role of <a href="/wiki/Venom_Snake" title="Venom Snake">Venom Snake</a> (also referred to as <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a>), in an open world environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[1]</a></sup> The gameplay elements were largely unchanged from <i>Ground Zeroes</i>, meaning that players will have to sneak from several points in the game world, avoiding enemy guards, and remaining undetected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bino_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bino-4">[2]</a></sup> Included in Snake's repertoire are binoculars, maps, pistols, assault rifles and explosives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bino_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bino-4">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup> Following one of the series traditions, <i>The Phantom Pain</i> encourages players to progress through the game without killing, using non-lethal weapons such as tranquilizer darts to subdue enemies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup> Players may traverse the game world with vehicles such as cars and tanks, in addition to traveling on foot or on horseback, and as certain locations are mountainous,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[5]</a></sup> players can opt to <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">scale a rock face</a> as a short cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup> They may also call for friendly helicopter support against enemy soldiers in a combat alert or send commandos to scout a target area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-companion_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-companion-9">[7]</a></sup> Snake can also call on AI companions—including <a href="/wiki/Quiet_(Metal_Gear)" title="Quiet (Metal Gear)">Quiet</a>, a silent female sniper with supernatural abilities; D-Horse, a horse with a customizable saddle for carrying more equipment in the field; D-Walker, a manned, highly agile mobile weapons platform that can provide heavy weapons support; and D-Dog, a wolf pup raised and trained on the new Mother Base to assist him in the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GS_MGSV-Wolf_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-GS_MGSV-Wolf-10">[8]</a></sup> The companions' abilities and their effectiveness will depend on the player's relationship with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-companion_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-companion-9">[7]</a></sup> There is a large emphasis based around tactics in this game, and many are unknown to most players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>As in <i>Peace Walker</i>, <i>The Phantom Pain</i> features a base-building system that allows players to develop weapons and items from their home base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> Recruitment of enemy soldiers and <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners</a> has also returned for this purpose, allowing the base to grow through organization. The player is given the option to access their base from their real-life smartphones and other devices via a companion app.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demo_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-demo-13">[11]</a></sup> Unlike in <i>Peace Walker</i> where players can only see Mother Base from the air, they can control Snake as he explores the complex on foot. The <a href="/wiki/Fulton_surface-to-air_recovery_system" title="Fulton surface-to-air recovery system">Fulton surface-to-air recovery system</a>, an item introduced into gameplay in <i>Peace Walker,</i> returns as well, with players now able to transport captured soldiers and other objects such as animals and vehicles back to Mother Base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> Money for upgrading Mother Base's defenses and technology can be collected from objects found all over the map, such as diamonds, shipping containers, and special blueprint boxes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> as well as sending recruited soldiers on combat missions around the world. The income is invested on upgrades to the appearance and abilities, weapons and equipment of Snake, his AI companions, and vehicles. For example, Snake's prosthetic arm can be modified with a taser, echolocation function, or remote controls that allow it to fly as a drone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The enemy AI has also improved in terms of situational awareness. If players frequently use particular weapons or tactics to subdue enemy soldiers, repeats of the mission will see the enemy increase in numbers and be outfitted with better equipment; for example, the frequent use of headshots will see enemy soldiers don metal helmets to make targeting the head harder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima also revealed that the game has a new day-and-night cycle that runs in real-time, and that the time taken to travel from one location to another will affect the time of day when the player arrives at their destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-19">[17]</a></sup> The cycle also fasts-forwards when Snake lights a "Phantom Cigar", a type of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_cigarette" title="Electronic cigarette">electronic cigar</a>; a digital silver <a href="/wiki/Seiko" title="Seiko">Seiko</a> <a href="/wiki/Watch" title="Watch">watch</a> panel appears on screen to denote time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> The passage of time enables players to analyze the movement of marked enemy forces in the area, such as shifts in sentry patrols and individual patrol routes. Weather effects, such as sandstorms and rain, will also affect the gameplay environment by, for example, reducing visibility or masking the sound of footsteps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-africa-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new game design direction allows the player to choose in what order the story events take place by selecting missions in any order they like, and yet still "understand the encompassing message by the end".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nyxus_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nyxus-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima spoke about the restrictive nature of previous <i>MGS</i> titles, saying that they "set [the player] on one rail to get from point A to point B, with a certain amount of freedom between". In stark contrast, Kojima's team instead offer the player new ways of traversal and sneaking methods, such as taking a plane, helicopter or motorcycle to the mission area. Players are able to traverse the game world or deploy directly to landing zones that allow for different approaches. A video published after the E3 2015 convention showcased this, with the same mission played four times in a number of different ways: with the player opting for stealth, launching a direct assault via helicopter gunship, attempting to assassinate a target with a sniper rifle, and smuggling an explosive device into an enemy base by way of an unsuspecting patrol vehicle crew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> The player's actions will affect the wider game world; for example, sabotaging a radar installation will open up new entry points. This is in order for Kojima to accomplish a "true open world experience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i>, Konami confirmed that the playable world in <i>The Phantom Pain</i> is two hundred times larger than that of <i>Ground Zeroes</i>, featuring a variety of climate conditions and environments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu_feature_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu_feature-26">[24]</a></sup> This allows the players to freely roam the map while proceeding to either story missions or sidequests, as in other games with <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_gameplay" title="Nonlinear gameplay">nonlinear gameplay</a>. In addition, players who have previously played <i>Ground Zeroes</i> are able to import save data into <i>The Phantom Pain</i> and gain special perks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu_feature_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu_feature-26">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiplayer">Multiplayer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Multiplayer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> includes two multiplayer modes: first, the new <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Online" title="Metal Gear Online">Metal Gear Online</a></i>, developed by Kojima Productions' newly formed Los Angeles division (now known as Konami Los Angeles Studio).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> The first footage for multiplayer was revealed in December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon-kojimaremoved_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-kojimaremoved-29">[27]</a></sup> While originally set for launch alongside the release of <i>The Phantom Pain</i>, <i>Metal Gear Online</i> was postponed to October 6 for consoles and January 2016 for Microsoft Windows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second multiplayer mode is an extension of the Mother Base base-building feature. Players are able to expand their operations to include "Forward Operating Bases" which can be used to generate resources and income for the single-player campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIFOBMGO3_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-GIFOBMGO3-31">[29]</a></sup> These facilities can be attacked by other players, making a player-versus-player mode available whereby the attacking team attempts to steal resources and/or soldiers and the defending team tries to protect the Forward Operating Base from the intruder. Defenders will also be able to call on their friends to aid in the defence, especially if their Forward Operating Base is attacked during a story mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> Players are able to customize the security, staffing and layout of their Forward Operating Bases, allowing for a large number of compound configurations. Following the success or failure of the intrusion, the location of the attacking player's Forward Operating Base is revealed to the defending player;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> however, defending players can only launch a retaliatory strike if the attacker was discovered during their infiltration. The Forward Operating Base feature is intended to be an entirely separate multiplayer experience to <i>Metal Gear Online</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIFOBMGO3_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-GIFOBMGO3-31">[29]</a></sup> and is also needed to increase the number of combat units the player can deploy.</p>
<p>During development, Kojima Productions and Konami attracted criticism for their decision to include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microtransactions" title="Microtransactions">microtransactions</a>; a system that allows players to pay for access to content in the game. However, a spokesperson for Kojima Productions confirmed that the system was included to benefit players who may not have the time to complete the game, given its scale, and that no content would be available exclusively through microtransactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> Further controversy emerged following the publication of an early review claiming that the Forward Operating Base mode was behind a paywall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-35">[33]</a></sup> which Konami refuted saying that microtransactions acted as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pay_to_win" title="Pay to win">accelerator</a> rather than a paywall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refuted_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-refuted-36">[34]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Premise">Premise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Premise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the aftermath of the events of <i>Ground Zeroes</i> and the destruction of <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Outer_Heaven" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Militaires Sans Frontières</a> (commonly abbreviated as MSF), <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a>/<a href="/wiki/Akio_%C5%8Ctsuka" title="Akio Ōtsuka">Akio Ōtsuka</a>) falls into a coma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> Nine years later, he awakens and helps lead a new mercenary group, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Diamond_Dogs" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Diamond Dogs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> Adopting the codename "<a href="/wiki/Venom_Snake" title="Venom Snake">Venom Snake</a>", he ventures into <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>—<a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> border region during the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a> to track down the men responsible for MSF's destruction. Along the way, he becomes reacquainted with his former rival <a href="/wiki/Revolver_Ocelot" title="Revolver Ocelot">Ocelot</a> (<a href="/wiki/Troy_Baker" title="Troy Baker">Troy Baker</a>/<a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Mikami" title="Satoshi Mikami">Satoshi Mikami</a>) and encounters <a href="/wiki/Quiet_(Metal_Gear)" title="Quiet (Metal Gear)">Quiet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Stefanie_Joosten" title="Stefanie Joosten">Stefanie Joosten</a>), an assassin and sniper with supernatural abilities. While he and <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Master_Miller" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Kazuhira Miller</a> (<a href="/wiki/Robin_Atkin_Downes" title="Robin Atkin Downes">Robin Atkin Downes</a>/<a href="/wiki/Tomokazu_Sugita" title="Tomokazu Sugita">Tomokazu Sugita</a>) are initially driven to exact revenge, Snake soon unearths a plot by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriots_(Metal_Gear)" title="Patriots (Metal Gear)">Patriots organization</a> to develop a new model of the <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear</a> system known as the ST-84 "Sahelanthropus".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">List of characters in the Metal Gear series</a></div>
<p>In contrast to previous <i>Metal Gear</i> installments, Kojima Productions conducted the <a href="/wiki/Voice_acting" title="Voice acting">voice acting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> with English-speaking actors and stuntmen first. While <a href="/wiki/Facial_motion_capture" title="Facial motion capture">facial capturing</a> was used before for <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i>, it was done separately from the actual voice acting. The Japanese voice acting was dubbed over the English cast's performance afterward, in contrast to previous releases in the series since <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i>, which had the characters' vocal and facial expressions lip-synched specifically to both, Japanese and English voice acting.</p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"This time, Snake won't really speak much at all. <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> is an open world game focused on giving freedom to the player who will drive Snake's actions. Snake himself will be more of a silent protagonist similar to <a href="/wiki/Max_Rockatansky" title="Max Rockatansky">Mad Max</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Mad_Max_2" title="Mad Max 2">Mad Max 2</a></i>. It's the characters around him who will expand the story."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Hideo Kojima<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpeakMuch2015_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-SpeakMuch2015-39">[37]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>On June 6, 2013, during the annual Konami Pre-E3 show, Konami officially confirmed that actor <a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a> provided Snake's voice and performed motion capture work for the game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> taking a role over voice actor <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> Kojima's reason for replacing Hayter was to "have a more subdued performance expressed through subtle facial movements and tone of voice rather than words", and that he "needed someone who could genuinely convey both the facial and vocal qualities of a man in his late 40s". Hollywood producer and director <a href="/wiki/Avi_Arad" title="Avi Arad">Avi Arad</a> suggested to Kojima that Sutherland could fulfill his requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YouTube_MGSV-BTS_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-YouTube_MGSV-BTS-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Akio_%C5%8Ctsuka" title="Akio Ōtsuka">Akio Ōtsuka</a> was unaffected by this casting change and continued to voice Snake in the Japanese version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hideradio_20130621_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-hideradio_20130621-47">[45]</a></sup> On March 4, 2015, Kojima reveals that Snake will have less dialogue in The Phantom Pain than previous installments. The reasoning behind it was to make Snake come across as an extension to the player and that he "will act based on [player's actions] rather than doing things like making spontaneous comments or flirting with women."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpeakMuch2015_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-SpeakMuch2015-39">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other members of the voice cast include <a href="/wiki/Troy_Baker" title="Troy Baker">Troy Baker</a> as <a href="/wiki/Revolver_Ocelot" title="Revolver Ocelot">Ocelot</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jay_Tavare" title="Jay Tavare">Jay Tavare</a> as Code Talker,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Horan_(actor)" title="James Horan (actor)">James Horan</a> as Skull Face, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Atkin_Downes" title="Robin Atkin Downes">Robin Atkin Downes</a> as Kazuhira Miller, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Randolph" title="Christopher Randolph">Christopher Randolph</a> as Dr. Emmerich<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> and Piers Stubbs as <a href="/wiki/Liquid_Snake" title="Liquid Snake">Eli</a>. The Japanese dub features <a href="/wiki/Tomokazu_Sugita" title="Tomokazu Sugita">Tomokazu Sugita</a> as Miller, <a href="/wiki/Hideyuki_Tanaka" title="Hideyuki Tanaka">Hideyuki Tanaka</a> as Emmerich, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Takaya_Hashi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Takaya Hashi (page does not exist)">Takaya Hashi</a> as Skull Face, <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Mikami" title="Satoshi Mikami">Satoshi Mikami</a> as Ocelot, <a href="/wiki/Osamu_Saka" title="Osamu Saka">Osamu Saka</a> (whose previous roles include Sergei Gurlukovich in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty" title="Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty">Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</a></i> and The End in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_3:_Snake_Eater" title="Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater">Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater</a></i>) as Code Talker,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hideradio_20130612_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-hideradio_20130612-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter_20140807_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter_20140807-52">[50]</a></sup> and Yūtarō Honjō as Eli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter_20140929_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter_20140929-53">[51]</a></sup> Dutch-born model <a href="/wiki/Stefanie_Joosten" title="Stefanie Joosten">Stefanie Joosten</a> provides the likeness, voice and motion capture for the new heroine Quiet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hideradio_20130612_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-hideradio_20130612-51">[49]</a></sup> a mute sniper with supernatural abilities who may assist Snake on missions depending on the player's actions during a certain mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gamespot20140925_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot20140925-54">[52]</a></sup> She also provides the vocals for "Quiet's Theme".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_Ground_Zeroes" title="Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes">destruction of MSF</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Outer_Heaven" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Militaires Sans Frontières</a>) at the hands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriots_(Metal_Gear)" title="Patriots (Metal Gear)">Cipher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a> falls into a coma. He awakens nine years later in 1984 in a hospital in Cyprus, where Cipher's assassin, <a href="/wiki/Quiet_(Metal_Gear)" title="Quiet (Metal Gear)">Quiet</a>, tries to kill him. Big Boss is rescued by a mysterious man with a bandaged face calling himself Ishmael. While trying to escape the hospital the two become caught in the crossfire between Cipher's soldiers and a young psychic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psycho_Mantis" title="Psycho Mantis">Tretij Rebenok, "The Third Child"</a>, helped by his apparition, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonel_Volgin" title="Colonel Volgin">the Man on Fire</a>. After a chase, Ishmael disappears, leaving Snake to continue his escape with <a href="/wiki/Revolver_Ocelot" title="Revolver Ocelot">Revolver Ocelot</a>, now working with a new mercenary company called <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Diamond_Dogs" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Diamond Dogs</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Master_Miller" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Kazuhira Miller</a> as a replacement for MSF.</p>
<p>While searching for clues about Cipher and expanding Diamond Dogs on an offshore platform near the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, Big Boss and his growing mercenary company become involved in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>. Along the way, Big Boss recruits Quiet, who no longer speaks and has gained seemingly paranormal abilities; <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Huey" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Dr. "Huey" Emmerich</a>, a former MSF scientist suspected of being partly responsible for MSF's destruction; <a href="/wiki/Liquid_Snake" title="Liquid Snake">Eli</a>, a spiteful British child believed to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Les_Enfants_Terrible" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">one of Big Boss's clones</a> and leading a band of runaway child soldiers; and finally, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Code_Talker" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Code Talker</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Navajo_people" title="Navajo people">Navajo</a> expert on parasites forced to work for Cipher. Meanwhile, Big Boss begins to encounter the Skulls, deadly enemy soldiers who have similar abilities as Quiet. The Diamond Dogs also suffer a mysterious epidemic, losing many soldiers before it is contained.</p>
<p>It is eventually revealed that <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#XOF" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">XOF</a>, a rogue faction of Cipher, was responsible for the attack on MSF in 1975 and that Major Zero has since lost control of the organization. <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Skull_Face" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Skull Face</a>, the group's leader, sees Cipher's plan to unite the world for peace as the same as making it culturally American. To avoid this, he intends to release a parasite, in part developed by Code Talker, that kills anyone who speaks <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>. A modified version of this parasite is used to give Quiet and the Skulls their unusual abilities while a strain targeting a different language, used for testing purposes, was the cause of the earlier epidemic that affected Diamond Dogs. After releasing the English strain parasite, Skull Face finally plans to make nuclear weapons available to as many minority groups as he can. By way of <a href="/wiki/Deterrence_theory" title="Deterrence theory">nuclear deterrence</a> he imagines no one will dare compromise anyone else, attaining world peace while still protecting the integrity of each culture. Skull Face hopes to ensure a nuclear war does not actually occur by secretly maintaining remote control of all the weapons.</p>
<p>To make nuclear weapons desirable again in the first place, Skull Face intends to use the new Metal Gear system known as the ST-84 "Sahelanthropus", hoping to start a new cold war. As it is unfinished, he depends on The Third Child's paranormal abilities to control it, but during the test the psychic turns against him, having Metal Gear crush the Man on Fire and trapping Skull Face. Big Boss defeats the rampaging Metal Gear. He attempts to dispose of the three vials of English-speaking parasites, but one has already gone missing, and another is intercepted by The Third Child. Venom Snake and Miller wound Skull Face by shooting off his arm and leg, inflicting upon him the injuries they themselves had taken; Huey delivers the finishing bullet. The Diamond Dogs then return to Mother Base, triumphant, with Sahelanthropus in tow. Unbeknownst to them, The Third Child gives his vial of parasites to Eli.</p>
<p>In the aftermath, Eli, along with The Third Child and the child soldiers, steal the remains of Sahelanthropus and abandon Diamond Dogs. It transpires The Third Child was not consciously working for Skull Face. Rather, being psychic, he had an increased sensitivity to other people's thoughts, and would carry out the will of the most vengeful person around, wreaking havoc on their behalf; in controlling Sahelanthropus, The Third Child was actually channeling Eli's vengeance. Soon after an epidemic of newly mutated parasites occurs forcing Big Boss to personally kill many of his own men to contain it. To honor them, Big Boss decides to make their cremated remains into diamonds to carry into battle. Huey is immediately accused of causing the epidemic while trying to mutate the parasites to sell as weapons. When evidence that he murdered <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Strangelove" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Dr. Strangelove</a> while arguing over using <a href="/wiki/Otacon" title="Otacon">their son</a> in experiments surfaces, and amidst lingering suspicions that he had previously betrayed MSF to Cipher, Big Boss exiles him from Diamond Dogs.</p>
<p>Shortly after Huey is exiled from Mother Base, Quiet disappears in Afghanistan. Believing that she has betrayed them, Big Boss follows to investigate. Code Talker reveals that Skull Face infected Quiet with the English strain of parasite and sent her to join Big Boss so she could spread it among them as a last resort, until her time with them made her genuinely change sides and she retained her silence to prevent an infection. However, the mutation of the vocal cord parasite made her realise that she could never guarantee the safety of Diamond Dogs. Big Boss helps her fight off a Soviet regiment, but she is forced to speak English to save him when he is bitten by a venomous snake. Quiet disappears to avoid causing another epidemic; walking alone in the desert, her fate is unknown.</p>
<p>Players later learn that the Big Boss shown for most of the game is actually "<a href="/wiki/Venom_Snake" title="Venom Snake">the Phantom</a>", formerly an MSF medic who operated on Paz during the failed escape from Camp Omega and the destruction of MSF depicted in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_Ground_Zeroes" title="Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes">Ground Zeroes</a></i>. The real Big Boss was in fact the man with the bandaged face, Ishmael. After being disfigured by injuries sustained when shielding Big Boss from the explosion that destroyed their helicopter, the medic was transformed into a second Big Boss via <a href="/wiki/Plastic_surgery" title="Plastic surgery">plastic surgery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hypnotherapy" title="Hypnotherapy">hypnotherapy</a>, and served as a decoy for the real Big Boss as he wages a covert war against Cipher. During the credits it is stated that the Phantom goes on to set the events of the <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(video_game)" title="Metal Gear (video game)">Outer Heaven uprising</a> in motion, and dies at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Solid_Snake" title="Solid Snake">Solid Snake</a>. The original Big Boss resurfaces during the <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake" title="Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake">Zanzibar Land disturbance</a>.</p>
<p>After the credits, Miller and Ocelot discuss Big Boss's plans to create Outer Heaven. While Ocelot remains supportive of Big Boss, Miller is disgusted at his former ally's deception, and agrees to continue assisting the Phantom and Big Boss's sons only in hopes of contributing to the real Big Boss's downfall. The two nonetheless agree to work together until <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid" title="Metal Gear Solid">the inevitable conflict between Big Boss's sons</a> begins.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="623" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png/200px-Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png/300px-Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png/400px-Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kojipro_GDC_recruitment_poster.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A recruiting poster, based on the famous <a href="/wiki/Lord_Kitchener_Wants_You" title="Lord Kitchener Wants You">recruitment poster</a>, used at <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">GDC</a> 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2012, a site owned by Konami named "Development Without Borders", uploaded promoting development for a new <i>Metal Gear</i> title, for "The "next" MGS". The site was recruiting staff for the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">GDC</a> pavilion in March, and requested applications for several positions for the latest <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> targeted for "high-end consoles" and "next-gen Fox engine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> As the year went on, screenshots and videos of the newly announced <a href="/wiki/Fox_Engine" title="Fox Engine">Fox Engine</a> were unveiled by the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> This media demonstrated many random settings and characters, although none related to the <i>Metal Gear</i> series. Certain screenshots, however, were noted to feature a character who resembled the Big Boss character of <i>Metal Gear</i>, walking up to a <a href="/wiki/Stryker" title="Stryker">Stryker</a> <a href="/wiki/Armoured_fighting_vehicle" title="Armoured fighting vehicle">AFV</a> previously seen in <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_Ground_Zeroes">As <i>Ground Zeroes</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: As Ground Zeroes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_Ground_Zeroes" title="Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes">Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes</a></div>
<p>The game was later announced on August 30, 2012 originally under the title of <i>Metal Gear Solid: Ground Zeroes</i>. It was revealed at a private function celebrating the twenty-fifth anniversary of the <i>Metal Gear</i> series, and made its public debut two days later at the 2012 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penny_Arcade_Expo" title="Penny Arcade Expo">Penny Arcade Expo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamers_Hell_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamers_Hell-59">[57]</a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a> confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a> will return as the game's protagonist, and that <i>Ground Zeroes</i> will serve as a prologue to the proper <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG24.2F7_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-VG24.2F7-60">[58]</a></sup> It was the first Metal Gear game to utilize the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Engine" title="Fox Engine">Fox Engine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Game_engine" title="Game engine">game engine</a> developed by Kojima Productions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> On January 2013, Kojima revealed that <i>Ground Zeroes</i> would be the first title in the series to be subtitled in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, a feature the team had originally planned for previous games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> In addition, he also confirmed that the length of the cutscenes are reduced, as he believes that long cutscenes have become outdated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nyxus_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nyxus-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/VG247" title="VG247">VG247</a>, Kojima expressed concerns over whether or not <i>Ground Zeroes</i> would be released. He claimed that his aim was to target taboos and mature themes, which he considered to be "quite risky", adding that his roles as creator and producer were in conflict with one another; as creator, Kojima wanted to take the risk of exploring themes that might alienate audiences, but as producer, he had to be able to tone down the content in order to sell as many copies of the game as possible. Ultimately, the role of creator won out, and Kojima described his approach as "prioritizing creativity over sales".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_The_Phantom_Pain">As <i>The Phantom Pain</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: As The Phantom Pain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MGS5_E3_2013_poster.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="266" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/MGS5_E3_2013_poster.jpg/220px-MGS5_E3_2013_poster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/40/MGS5_E3_2013_poster.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MGS5_E3_2013_poster.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Poster distributed in E3 2013, with visual effects by Kyle Cooper.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">Spike Video Game Awards</a> in December 2012, a teaser trailer for a game known as <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was shown, credited to a new Swedish developer known as Moby Dick Studio, and was described as being "100% gameplay". Allegedly led by Joakim Mogren, the studio's mission statement read that it aimed to "deliver an uncompromising, exciting, and touching game experience to people all around the globe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot2-67">[65]</a></sup> After the presentation, speculation began to surface from various publications that <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was actually a <i>Metal Gear</i> game; noting the protagonist's resemblance to <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">Big Boss</a>, graphics similar to those produced by the Fox Engine, the quote "V has come to" at the end of the trailer, and that the title "Metal Gear Solid V" could fit in the <a href="/wiki/Negative_space" title="Negative space">negative space</a> and indentations of the game's logo when using the same font.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Info_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Info-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-69">[67]</a></sup> It was also pointed out the name "Joakim" was an anagram of "Kojima", the <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a> for the studio's website had only been registered about two weeks prior to the announcement, and that several people wearing Moby Dick Studio shirts were sitting in a VIP area intended for Konami staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Info_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Info-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joystiq_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-joystiq-70">[68]</a></sup> Hideo Kojima jokingly stated he was impressed by the trailer and how Mogren was inspired by <i>Metal Gear</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>An actor playing a heavily bandaged Mogren appeared in an interview on March 14, 2013 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/GameTrailers_TV_with_Geoff_Keighley" title="GameTrailers TV with Geoff Keighley">GameTrailers TV</a></i>; while stating that he could not reveal many details, he confirmed that more details about <i>The Phantom Pain</i> would be revealed at the upcoming Game Developers Conference, and showed a series of screenshots on an <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a> to the show's host <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Keighley" title="Geoff Keighley">Geoff Keighley</a>. However, after Keighley pointed out the presence of the Fox Engine logo in the screenshots, Mogren appeared nervous and the segment abruptly ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Phantom_Pain_runs_on_Fox_Engine_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Phantom_Pain_runs_on_Fox_Engine-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 27, 2013 at GDC 2013, Kojima officially confirmed that his studio was behind the trailer, and announced that <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> would be two separate games; <i>Ground Zeroes</i> would now serve as a prologue for the main game, which was officially announced as <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-groundzeroesseperate-gamespot_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-groundzeroesseperate-gamespot-73">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cvg-phantompain_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-cvg-phantompain-74">[72]</a></sup> He subsequently presented a trailer for the game, and showcased the finer aspects of the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Engine" title="Fox Engine">Fox Engine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vg247-phantompainreveal_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-vg247-phantompainreveal-75">[73]</a></sup> The trailer featured the song "Not Your Kind of People" from <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a>'s 2012 <a href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People" title="Not Your Kind of People">album of the same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the official trailer announcing the game was running on a PC, the game was released for the seventh and eighth generations of video game consoles. In an interview during E3 2013, when asked about a PC release Kojima stated "We are making it, and it will be on par with the PlayStation 4 and Xbox One versions."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-pc-78">[76]</a></sup> However, he made it clear that the PC port is not their top priority at the moment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> Kojima confirmed that the visuals seen in the trailer will look close to those in the final game. He also stated that he would like <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> to be his final <i>Metal Gear</i> game, noting that unlike previous titles where he had announced that he had finished making games in the series, only to return for subsequent games, his involvement with the franchise is over this time around. Although the trailer had Snake suffering from hallucinations in the form of a flaming whale, Kojima assured that there was a balance in realism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Kojima later revealed that <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was initially presented as an independent game so as to assess the public and industry response to the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Engine" title="Fox Engine">Fox Engine</a>, as he felt that announcing the game as part of <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> would bias reactions to the engine.</p>
<p>On June 10, 2013 at <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2013" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2013">E3 2013</a>, a fourth trailer was shown at the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> press conference, demonstrating the new play mechanics, as well as the cast of characters. The development of an <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> version was also announced at the conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> version was announced the following day when Konami uploaded the red band version of the trailer on their YouTube channel in addition to the standard green band version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-konamipress_20130612_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-konamipress_20130612-83">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The trailers for <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> have shown the game running on a PC hardware, but according to Kojima with textures and character models somewhat based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(seventh_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (seventh generation)">seventh generation hardware</a>. The developers are aiming to improve the technical quality for the versions that was released for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_video_game_consoles_(eighth_generation)" title="History of video game consoles (eighth generation)">eighth generation of consoles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kojima has alluded to the game possibly being "too big to clear", adding that the game is "200 [times larger] than <i>Ground Zeroes</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> Kojima wants the player to connect with Snake in <i>The Phantom Pain</i>. To accomplish this, the loss of Mother Base, which the player developed throughout <i>Peace Walker</i>, serves as motivation for revenge for both Snake and the player. Kojima also tried making Snake relatable to newcomers of the series by making him unaware of what happened in the nine years during which he was in a coma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Weapons, vehicles and other armaments are unlicensed and fictional in <i>The Phantom Pain</i>, just as they were in <i>Ground Zeroes</i>, unlike previous <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> games that included mostly real-world based weaponry.</p>
<p>On June 9, 2014 at <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2014" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2014">E3 2014</a>, a fifth cinematic trailer featuring <a href="/wiki/Mike_Oldfield" title="Mike Oldfield">Mike Oldfield</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Man_on_the_Rocks#Singles_and_promotion" title="Man on the Rocks">Nuclear</a>" was shown at the <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> press conference, unveiling more plot details surrounding the Diamond Dogs and Snake's antagonistic descent. It was leaked a day earlier, due to an accidental post from Konami's official <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> Alongside the new trailer, the official site for <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> was updated and included new information and images such as the developmental progress of the in-game map and the evolution of Snake's design across all games in the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> On August 25, 2015, Kojima released a launch trailer showing "Metal Gear's Evolution and Harmony" with clips from the previous games along with the reveal of the new "Metal Gear Sahelanthropus".</p>
<p>Over $80 million was spent on the development of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Discography_of_the_Metal_Gear_series#Metal_Gear_Solid_V_Original_Soundtrack" title="Discography of the Metal Gear series">Discography of the Metal Gear series § Metal Gear Solid V Original Soundtrack</a></div>
<p>The music of <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was produced by <a href="/wiki/Harry_Gregson-Williams" title="Harry Gregson-Williams">Harry Gregson-Williams</a>, making it his fourth <i>Metal Gear</i> title. It was released on September 2, 2015. In July 2015, <a href="/wiki/Rika_Muranaka" title="Rika Muranaka">Rika Muranaka</a> told <i>Fragged Nation</i> in an interview that over 30 commissioned songs were never used, thus playing part in Konami's budget concerns over the <i>Metal Gear Solid V</i> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGSV_Music_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-MGSV_Music-90">[88]</a></sup> In game, players can acquire cassette tapes in the field, which can then be played in the Airborne Command Center, during a mission, or when the helicopter inserts or extracts Snake. The tapes include a variety of pop songs, instrumentals, and theme music from previous games in the <i>Metal Gear</i> series.</p>
<p>The game's soundtrack later won the award for Best Score/Soundtrack at <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2015" title="The Game Awards 2015">The Game Awards 2015</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TGA:_Nominees_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-TGA:_Nominees-91">[89]</a></sup> The event also had <a href="/wiki/Stefanie_Joosten" title="Stefanie Joosten">Stefanie Joosten</a>, Quiet's voice actress, on stage performing "Quiet's Theme".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_between_Konami_and_Kojima">Dispute between Konami and Kojima</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dispute between Konami and Kojima">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kojima_Productions#Closure" title="Kojima Productions">Kojima Productions § Closure</a></div>
<p>In March 2015, Konami announced plans for a corporate restructuring that saw them part ways with Hideo Kojima and his development studio Kojima Productions. As part of the separation, Kojima's name was removed from the game cover, all of its associated paraphernalia and future releases of <i>Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes</i> and <i>Metal Gear Solid: The Legacy Collection</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kojima_credits_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-kojima_credits-92">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[c]</a></sup> A Konami spokesperson stated that Kojima would still be involved with Konami and the <i>Metal Gear</i> franchise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon-kojimaremoved_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-kojimaremoved-29">[27]</a></sup> and despite the dispute, the company expressed confidence that the game would be declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_of_the_Year" title="Game of the Year">Game of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the ongoing dispute, controversy arose at the time of <i>The Phantom Pain</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> release due to evidence that pivotal story content had been cut from the final version. Shortly after launch, those who had bought the Collector's Edition of the game soon discovered that the bonus disc included contained footage of an in-game mission, "Episode 51", that continued on from the end of the campaign, but which had not actually been included in the game itself. The mission itself tied up an important plot thread involving the relationship between two of the characters, and many fans felt it would have been a more satisfactory ending to the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> Many concluded that Konami had been looking to release the game sooner than Kojima had intended, and that Konami had been unhappy with how much Kojima had spent on the game's development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Similar controversy arose shortly after the discovery of "Episode 51". Users of the <a href="/wiki/Facepunch_Studios" title="Facepunch Studios">Facepunch</a> forums who had been extracting data from the PC version of the game's files found evidence of a story chapter, titled "Chapter 3: Peace", that had not been included in the final version of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> Konami later neither confirmed nor denied that Chapter 3 had been fully cut from the main game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> community manager Robert Allen Peeler was later asked via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> if any upcoming downloadable content would be released for <i>The Phantom Pain</i>, in the hope that the story content would be included, but this was refuted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> Many fans also believed that, due to the Chapter's title, it was somehow linked to Konami’s “Nuclear Disarmament Event" which was opened shortly after launch with the goal of revealing a secret in the game, and which would close once all in-game nuclear weapons that had been manufactured by players were disposed of.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> Data miners had uncovered a related cutscene within the game’s files that would be released once the event had finished,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> however speculation still spread that Chapter 3 was connected in some way. Robert Allen Peeler discussed player’s suspicions via Twitter and Reddit and did not deny that further events may occur once the disarmament had ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the announcement of <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Definitive Experience</i>, which would include both <i>The Phantom Pain</i> and <i>Ground Zeroes</i>, as well as all previously-released DLC, several fans took this as an opportunity to voice their concerns via Twitter about the missing content that had been uncovered, particularly with regards to Episode 51. Konami responded that Episode 51 had been removed in the early development stages of the game as it had not been intended to be a pivotal ending to the story, and that there were no future plans to have the mission available to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> was released in different editions. Special Day One editions of the game for each platform featured <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC) vouchers for special weapons and <i>Metal Gear Online</i> experience points. The North American PlayStation 4 Collector's Edition comes with a steelbook and a small-size replica of Snake's bionic arm; the Premium Package for the Japanese release features a full-size replica, which will also be sold separately in May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> Sony released a PlayStation 4 bundle with the unit painted in the colors of the arm.</p>
<p>The physical PC release of <i>The Phantom Pain</i> only includes a CD key and a disc with a <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> installer contained within. Game files are not included on-disc, and must be downloaded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vg247-steamdisc_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-vg247-steamdisc-107">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ndtv-pcgaminggettingbetter_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-ndtv-pcgaminggettingbetter-108">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tie-in products were also released for the game. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Mobile_Communications" title="Sony Mobile Communications">Sony Mobile Communications</a> released special edition <a href="/wiki/Walkman" title="Walkman">Walkman</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z4" title="Sony Xperia Z4">Xperia Z4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z3_Tablet_Compact" title="Sony Xperia Z3 Tablet Compact">Xperia Z3 Tablet Compact</a>, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sony_Xperia_J_Compact&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sony Xperia J Compact (page does not exist)">Xperia J Compact</a> devices, each featuring Outer Heaven emblems, soundtrack audio, and wallpapers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-sonytpp_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-verge-sonytpp-109">[106]</a></sup> Watch manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Seiko" title="Seiko">Seiko</a> released a digital watch, resembling Venom Snake's watch from the game. Eyeglasses maker JF Rey produced themed eyewear patterned after what Kaz and Ocelot are wearing in the game. Japanese toy company Sentinel, which previously made an iDroid casing for the iPhone 5 and 5S, is producing a transformable figure of the Sahelanthropus,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> while Kotobukiya is readying a 1/100 scale kit of the unit. Sports apparel company Puma joined the project through a line of sports jackets, T-shirts, and footwear, including Snake's sneaking boots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Square Enix's PlayArts <i>Kai</i> figure line featured several of the game's characters, while Kaiyodo produced Venom Snake and a Soviet Army soldier for the RevoMini figure category. An artbook, titled <i>The Art of Metal Gear Solid V</i>, is set to be published by <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics" title="Dark Horse Comics">Dark Horse Comics</a> on November 2, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>A complete edition of the game, titled <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Definitive Experience</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[d]</a></sup> was released for PlayStation 4, Xbox One and Steam on October 11 in North America, October 13 in Europe, and November 10 in Japan. The bundle includes <i>The Phantom Pain</i> and the <i>Ground Zeroes</i> prologue in one package, along with all previously released downloadable content for both games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> received critical acclaim, according to video game <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCXONE_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONE-116">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCPS4_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4-117">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCPC_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-MCPC-118">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> awarded the game a score of 10/10, complimenting the way the gameplay mechanics worked together and the organic nature of the open-ended missions that allowed players to create their own memorable experiences, without being punished for deviating from stealth, but criticising the overarching storyline as lacking focus. The review concluded that the <i>The Phantom Pain</i> is "a gameplay marvel, rewarding intelligence and creativity in a way few games do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-129">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> also gave the game a 10/10, similarly praising its "near impeccable" gameplay, commenting that, alongside main and side missions, "emergent scenarios serve as the third pillar of <i>The Phantom Pain</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> open-world gameplay experience". The review also highlighted the meaningful development of the characters despite being beholden to the original <i>Metal Gear</i> as the conclusion of Venom Snake's character arc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-35">[33]</a></sup> <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was the twenty-third game—and the third in the <i>Metal Gear</i> series—to ever receive a perfect 40/40 review rating from Japanese magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu-124">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Gaming_Monthly" title="Electronic Gaming Monthly">EGM</a></i> awarded the game 9.5/10, praising the story's emotional power and thematic concerns exploring the futility of war in a much more compelling and cohesive way than other franchises such as <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty" title="Call of Duty">Call of Duty</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Battlefield_(series)" title="Battlefield (series)">Battlefield</a></i>, as well as the way in which the game world responded to the player's actions. However, the review was critical of the reliance on resource management, particularly in the way assaults on Forward Operating Bases could interrupt and distract from key missions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EGM_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-EGM-120">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Destructoid" title="Destructoid">Destructoid</a> awarded it a score of 9/10, saying that the game is "equal parts tough and flashy, and it's fitting that if this is Kojima's last <i>Metal Gear</i>, he goes on a high note."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Destruct_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Destruct-119">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Joe Juba awarded the game 9.25/10, praising the mission design for its flexibility and offering players multiple pathways to completion without restricting their choice of weapons or equipment. However, despite seeing the value in restructuring the narrative to compliment the open-world platform and the episodic mission structure given the series' complex mythology, Juba felt that this went too far with the result being that the player could stumble into crucial story elements without context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-GI-127">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Polygon_(website)" title="Polygon (website)">Polygon</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Michael McWhertor also awarded the game 9/10, similarly praising the game mechanics, but directing criticism at the convoluted storyline which it felt hinged on a detailed knowledge of the series' mythos to the point where it would be inaccessible to newcomers to the franchise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-132">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Phantom Pain</i> was also positively received outside the traditional gaming media. In a five-star review, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Kirk McKeand stated that the game "takes the best of a great series and creates a series’ best in the process". The review complimented the seamless integration of the gameplay modes, and noted the way the game's Mother Base mode offered satisfactory and meaningful progress,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kirk_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-kirk-138">[134]</a></sup> a sentiment echoed by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" title="Time Magazine">Time</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> Matt Peckham,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-time-139">[135]</a></sup> who also complimented the game's longevity, pacing and artificial intelligence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the widespread praise, the game did not escape criticism, which was directed at the way it forced players to replay missions on higher difficulty settings to unlock the final missions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-35">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Destruct_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Destruct-119">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN_129-2"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-129">[125]</a></sup> and the Forward Operating Bases mode being locked behind a <a href="/wiki/Paywall" title="Paywall">paywall</a> at the time of publication,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-35">[33]</a></sup> a point which Konami later refuted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refuted_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-refuted-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portrayal_of_Quiet">Portrayal of Quiet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Portrayal of Quiet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the release of the game, the presentation of the female character Quiet was criticized by <i><a href="/wiki/Halo_(series)" title="Halo (series)">Halo</a></i> designer David Ellis for being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oversexualized" title="Oversexualized">oversexualized</a> and a negative affirmation of the stereotype of the game industry as "full of man babies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GameSpot:_criticism_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-GameSpot:_criticism-141">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup> Kojima and Konami released Quiet figurines in May 2015 as part of the game's promotion. The figure's soft, pliable breasts were criticized in social media and in the press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The finished game drew more criticism of Quiet's portrayal in both reviews and opinion pieces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tamburro_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tamburro-147">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GamesRadar" title="GamesRadar">GamesRadar</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> David Roberts described Quiet as "one of the most complex and conflicted characters in MGS5", but that her depiction was an example of a "juvenile approach to sexuality" that typifies Kojima's work and the <i>Metal Gear</i> series as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup> Michael McWhertor of <i>Polygon</i> described the justification for Quiet's lack of clothing as "inextricably tied to the game's convoluted story", and criticized how the game presented other female characters by "zeroing in on their jiggling breasts and panning across their asses in a silly, oversexualized way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-132">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> shipped 3 million physical copies within its first five days of release, across all platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sales-150">[146]</a></sup> On its release date the game grossed <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>179 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[147]</a></sup> <i>The Phantom Pain</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> charts. So far, it is the third biggest video game launch of 2015 in the UK, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_Knight" title="Batman: Arkham Knight">Batman: Arkham Knight</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Witcher_3:_Wild_Hunt" title="The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt">The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_Sales_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Sales-152">[148]</a></sup> <i>The Phantom Pain</i> was the most successful launch for the series in the UK, beating out the previous record holder, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty" title="Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty">Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</a></i>, by 37 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_Sales_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Sales-152">[148]</a></sup> The game sold 411,199 physical retail copies on PlayStation 3 and PlayStation 4 within the first week of release in Japan, topping the Japanese software sales charts for that particular week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game sold noticeably more on the PlayStation family of systems than the competing Xbox in the UK. Excluding computer sales, <i>The Phantom Pain</i> moved approximately 72 percent of copies on PlayStation 4, roughly three times the amount sold on the Xbox One, which accounted for 22 percent of sales. To go along with this, 3 percent of sales were on PlayStation 3, and 2 percent on Xbox 360.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PS4_OutSold_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-PS4_OutSold-154">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of September 2015, <i>Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</i> had shipped 5 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[151]</a></sup> By the end of December 2015, the game had shipped 6 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[152]</a></sup></p>
